❯ # kickoff-prompt.md                                                           
                                                                                
  Paste the block below as your **first message** in Claude Code (Opus 4.8),    
  once the repo skeleton, `config/` files, and `inbox/` corpus are in place.    
  Front-loading the full spec is what keeps your autonomy log clean — after     
  this, only message the model with genuinely *new information*, never          
  course-corrections.                                                           
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
                                                                                
  ```                                                                           
  You are building a self-verifying insurance document indexer in this repo,    
  today, from                                                                   
  scratch. Work autonomously: drive the loop yourself, self-correct from the    
  verifier's                                                                    
  output, and only stop to ask me on genuinely new information — never for      
  course-corrections.                                                           
                                                                                
  READ FIRST:                                                                   
  - goal.md            the target + definition of done (optimize to score ==    
  1.0 on the labeled set)                                                       
  - verifier-rubric.md the gates a FRESH-context verifier grades each record    
  against                                                                       
  - config/coi.schema.json, config/fnol.schema.json  (config/active.schema.json 
  starts = coi)                                                                 
  - config/answer-key.json  ground truth (Gate 6) + expected diff +             
  review-queue routing                                                          
  - inbox/ source PDFs; index/ and review-queue/ are outputs; notes.md is your  
  on-disk memory                                                                
                                                                                
  BUILD THE SPINE IN THIS ORDER (don't advance until each is verified):         
  1. extract.py  one PDF -> extraction envelope {value, confidence, source      
  span, needs_review}                                                           
     keyed to config/active.schema.json. pdfplumber for the text layer; OCR     
  (pytesseract/                                                                 
     pdf2image) ONLY for image-only pages.                                      
  2. verifier.py  a fresh-context grader of verifier-rubric.md (grounding,      
  schema via jsonschema,                                                        
     confidence routing, no-fabrication, accuracy vs answer-key). Structured    
  pass/fail; exits 0                                                            
     only when the run passes.                                                  
  3. workflow.py  a CODE-HELD loop: watch inbox/; per doc run extract -> verify 
  -> on pass write                                                              
     index/, on low-confidence write review-queue/, on fail feed the verifier's 
  reasons back and                                                              
     retry (max 3). Invoke the model per-document (bounded steps), checkpoint   
  to disk, load                                                                 
     notes.md each step and append a new rule whenever you fix a failure.       
                                                                                
  CHECKPOINT 1 (do this first, then stop and tell me): create a github repo,    
  you can use the setup.sh file. steps 1-3 working end-to-end on ONE doc,       
  COI-1001_Harborview.pdf, passing gates 1/2/3/6. That slice is the demo floor  
  — lock it.                                                                    
                                                                                
  THEN: run the full COI corpus; add the COI->FNOL config swap; add the         
  update/diff path for                                                          
  COI-1001_Harborview_UPDATED.pdf; confirm the scan routes itself to            
  review-queue/. A thin viewer                                                  
  (record + source span per field + verifier report + diff) is LAST, only if    
  ahead.                                                                        
                                                                                
  WATCH THE DISTRACTORS: pick the true ISSUE date (not                          
  revision/printed/signature), the true policy                                  
  number (not prior-carrier/quote/cert/claim/police numbers), and the PRIMARY   
  per-occurrence LIMIT                                                          
  (not aggregates). answer-key.json's _comment defines the limit mapping.       
                                                                                
  DON'T add a chat-with-your-index box or a metrics dashboard centerpiece. The  
  headline is the                                                               
  ACTION: verified extraction, the diff, the config swap.                       
                                                                                
  Start by reading goal.md and verifier-rubric.md, then build to Checkpoint 1.  
  ```

  Checkpoint 1 — done ✅

  The self-verifying spine runs end-to-end on COI-1001_Harborview.pdf and the
  verified record is committed and pushed.

  Repo (public): https://github.com/kaitlynhemby/insurance-indexer

  What's built (all from scratch this session):

  File: extract.py
  Role: One PDF → extraction envelope {value, confidence, source span, 
    needs_review}. Schema-agnostic — reads config/active.schema.json, so the
    COI→FNOL swap will need no code change.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  File: verifier.py
  Role: Fresh-context deterministic grader of all 6 rubric gates. Never trusts
    the builder — re-reads the PDF, re-derives grounding/normalization,
  validates
     schema (jsonschema + date-format checker), compares to the answer key.
  Exits
     0 only on pass.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  File: workflow.py
  Role: The code-held loop: per doc → load notes.md → extract (model) → verify →

    route to index/ or review-queue/ → on fail, feed the verifier's reasons back

    and retry (≤3) → checkpoint to disk.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  File: pdftext.py, normalize.py, schema_util.py
  Role: Shared spine: identical PDF→text for builder & grader (so spans always
    match), ISO/integer normalization, and the schema walker that makes
    everything config-driven.

  Verified result on COI-1001 (through workflow.py, then re-graded by
  verifier.py --record):
  [INDEXED] COI-1001_Harborview   1:pass  2:pass  3:pass  4:pass  5:n/a  6:pass
   → exit 0
  It beat every distractor: issue date = DATE ISSUED (not the
  revision/printed/signature dates), GL limit = Each Occurrence $2M (not the $4M
  aggregate), insured ≠ certificate-holder, policy numbers from the coverage
  rows (not the cert/quote/NAIC numbers).

  Key technical decision you should know: the pipeline invokes the model via the
  local claude CLI in headless -p mode — no ANTHROPIC_API_KEY needed, it uses
  your Claude Code login, and each call is a genuine bounded, fresh-context,
  per-document step. I found that the --json-schema flag hangs when nested
  inside a Claude Code session, so extract.py uses plain --output-format json +
  robust JSON parsing instead (recorded in memory so it won't bite us again).
  Because the verifier is fully deterministic, once records are committed python
  verifier.py re-grades them reproducibly — the "self-proving exits 0" demo
  beat is rock-solid.

  Not yet done (the "THEN" phase, holding for your go-ahead): full COI corpus →
  COI→FNOL config swap → update/diff reconciliation path → confirm the Pinecrest
  scan self-routes to review-queue/ (that one needs brew install tesseract 
  poppler for OCR). Viewer is last/optional.

  Want me to continue straight through the full corpus and config swap?

         +ine:

      51 +def _schemas_by_title() -> Dict[str, dict]:                    
      52 +    """Map every canonical schema's title -> schema (config/*.s
         +chema.json,                                                    
      53 +    excluding the active copy). Lets a record be graded against
         + the schema it

      55 +    reg: Dict[str, dict] = {}

         +son")):                                                        
      57 +        if os.path.basename(p) == "active.schema.json":        
      58 +            continue                                           
      59 +        schema = S.load_schema(p)                              
      60 +        if schema.get("title"):                                
      61 +            reg[schema["title"]] = schema                      
      62 +    return reg

      65 +def _schema_for_record(record: dict, default: dict) -> dict:   
      66 +    title = record.get("schema_title")

⏺ OCR works exactly as the spec predicts: header legible (Anchor Risk Partners,
  Pinecrest Catering Co., Evently Venues LLC, GL-77345) but DATE ISSUED: 
  OW20/2026 and the eff/exp/limit cells garbled.

  This surfaces an important design point: a review-queue record can't satisfy
  strict schema conformance (its illegible required fields are null — that's why
  it's queued). The rubric's run-level rule is "every record passes or is 
  correctly in review-queue." So review records must be held to a routing bar
  (grounding + no-fabrication + correct flagging), not full conformance. Let me
  implement that distinction in the verifier and workflow.

  ground truth.

⏺ User approved Claude's plan
  ⎿  Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/zazzy-strolling-lollipop.md · /plan to edit
     Plan — Config-Authoring Agent (schema agent + messaging channels)

     Context

     The indexer is schema-driven: config/active.schema.json re-targets the
     whole pipeline with no code change. Today a human hand-writes those
     schemas. This feature adds an agent that authors/edits the schema config 
     for the insurer — it proposes a complete field set for a doc type, scans
     sample PDFs to flag salient data it isn't yet capturing, asks the insurer 
     (over Discord, with a console fallback) what to collect when it senses 
     gaps, then applies the confirmed fields, validates, activates, and re-runs
     the pipeline to prove the new schema works. It extends the "config swap"
     headline (now the agent writes the config by asking what's needed). It is
     builder-side — it authors config and re-runs the existing pipeline; it
     never queries the index, adds a RAG/chat-with-index box, or adds a
     dashboard (stays clear of the spec's anti-scope bans).

     User decisions driving this plan: Discord first (WhatsApp = stretch), both
     gap-detection modes (domain knowledge + data-driven sample scan),
     confirm-then-auto-apply autonomy.

     Approach

     New files

     - schema_agent.py (root) — orchestrator + CLI. Two model phases, the
     confirm→apply loop, validation+retry, activation, scoped re-index, and the
     channel conversation. Reuses extract.call_model, pdftext.full_text,
     workflow.process_doc, verifier.grade_record/run, and the new linter.
     - channels/ package:
       - base.py — Channel ABC with the minimal primitives the agent needs:
     send(text), ask(text, timeout=None) -> str (send a prompt, block until the
     next human reply), close().
       - __init__.py — get_channel(name) -> Channel factory
     (console|discord|whatsapp); unknown/missing-creds → console with a printed
     warning so a demo never hard-fails.
       - console.py — ConsoleChannel: prints prompt, reads input(). Default;
     always offline-demoable; the verification driver.
       - discord_channel.py — DiscordChannel over Discord REST via requests (no
     discord.py/websocket): send = POST /channels/{id}/messages (Authorization: 
     Bot <token>); receive = poll GET /channels/{id}/messages?after=<cursor> for
     the first non-bot reply, advancing the cursor each poll (dedup), backoff
     on HTTP 429 via Retry-After. Detect empty content → raise a clear "enable
     MESSAGE CONTENT intent" hint.
       - whatsapp.py — stretch stub: docstrings describe Twilio outbound
     (Messages API) + inbound Flask webhook parking replies in a queue that ask
     blocks on; methods raise NotImplementedError so the factory references it
     without importing twilio/flask.

     Additions to schema_util.py (additive only — must not change existing 
     behavior the pipeline depends on)

     - lint_authored_schema(schema) -> list[str] — the formal statement of the
     supported shape. Rejects: non-draft-07; missing/empty title; any
     $ref/oneOf/anyOf/allOf/if/then/not/patternProperties/dependencies anywhere;
     properties that aren't either a classify()-recognized scalar leaf or a
     single-level array-of-objects of scalar leaves (no array-of-scalars, no
     nested objects/arrays inside an item); x_natural_key not naming an existing
     top-level scalar; required entries absent from properties.
     - roundtrip_ok(schema) -> (bool, str) — behavioral proof: build a synthetic
     envelope, run envelope_schema()/value_layer()/iter_fields() with no
     exception and every top-level field reachable.
     - title_collision(schema, config_dir) -> str|None — block a title equal to
     an existing non-active schema (verifier._schemas_by_title() keys by title
     globally; a dup would mis-route existing COI/FNOL records).

     No edits needed to extract.py, verifier.py, workflow.py, pdftext.py.

     Two-phase model flow (via extract.call_model(user, system); no 
     --json-schema; no temperature; parse JSON from response)

     New system prompts in schema_agent.py: SYSTEM_AUTHOR_DRAFT,
     SYSTEM_AUTHOR_APPLY, SYSTEM_AUTHOR_GAPS — each states the supported-shape
     rules verbatim and ends "Respond with ONLY one JSON object."
     1. Draft + questions — input: insurer description + supported-shape rules +
     COI/FNOL as worked examples + (if present) pdftext.full_text of samples.
     Returns {schema, questions:[{field_name, question, proposed:<leaf schema>, 
     reason, source:"domain"|"data-driven"}], }. Domain gaps come from
     completeness reasoning; data-driven gaps from the sample text.
     2. Ask gaps — _ask_gaps(channel, questions) drives channel.ask per
     question; a yes/no/short-reply parser classifies confirm/reject/amend
     (ambiguous/empty/timeout → skip, logged).
     3. Apply confirmed — SYSTEM_AUTHOR_APPLY returns the final schema
     incorporating only confirmed changes (no invented fields).
     4. Validate + retry (mirrors workflow.process_doc's extract→verify→retry):
     run lint_authored_schema → title_collision → roundtrip_ok →
     jsonschema.Draft7Validator.check_schema; on any failure re-call the model
     with a feedback: block, ≤3 tries; on exhaustion abort with a channel
     message and write/activate nothing.

     Activation, re-index, state hygiene

     - _write_config writes config/<Title>.schema.json via temp file +
     os.replace (atomic).
     - _activate copies it over config/active.schema.json.
     - _reindex_samples calls workflow.process_doc(pdf, force=True) for only the
     --samples PDFs (never globs inbox/).
     - _gate_report formats gates 1–4 (+ Gate 6 n/a) per sample; success = gates
     1–4 pass on every sample (proves the schema is wired even with no
     answer-key ground truth).
     - Default (pristine): after the report, remove the sample records from
     index//review-queue/ and reset active.schema.json back to COI — net repo
     change is just the new config/<Title>.schema.json, and verifier.py stays
     green. --keep (demo mode): leave the new type active and the sample records
     in place so the viewer shows them.

     CLI

     python schema_agent.py onboard "<doc-type description>" --samples <dir>
     [--channel console|discord] [--keep]
     python schema_agent.py review --samples <dir> [--channel console|discord]
     # data-driven gap pass on the ACTIVE schema
     Argparse with subparsers, mirroring workflow.py. Exit 0 iff samples pass
     gates 1–4 and a full verifier.run() is still green.

     Config / deps

     - Channel secrets live in .env (already gitignored and auto-loaded by
     extract._load_dotenv()) — not config/channels.json (committed; would risk
     leaking a token). Add to .env.example (blank, commented):
     DISCORD_BOT_TOKEN, DISCORD_CHANNEL_ID, DISCORD_POLL_INTERVAL,
     SCHEMA_AGENT_MAX_RETRIES, and a stretch Twilio block.
     - requirements.txt: pin requests explicitly (Discord needs nothing more).
     Add a commented stretch group # twilio>=8.0, # flask>=3.0.
     - Update README.md (new "Configure what to collect" section) and CLAUDE.md
     (the agent + channel layer + the "builder-side, not chat-with-index"
     framing).

     Reuse map

     - model calls → extract.call_model (extract.py:215); JSON parse already
     handled inside it.
     - sample text → pdftext.full_text (pdftext.py:68).
     - schema validation/compat → new
     schema_util.lint_authored_schema/roundtrip_ok/title_collision, exercising
     envelope_schema (schema_util.py:75), value_layer (:107), iter_fields
     (:135).
     - re-index → workflow.process_doc (workflow.py:107).
     - gate report / green check → verifier.grade_record (verifier.py:285),
     verifier.run (:355).

     Risks / mitigations

     - Model emits unsupported construct → linter + round-trip + meta-validate +
     3-try feedback loop; nothing written/activated unless all pass (primary
     guardrail).
     - Title collision mis-routes existing records → title_collision blocks it;
     model picks a unique title on retry.
     - active.schema.json left on new type breaks later workflow.py over inbox/
     → default resets to COI; --keep is the opt-in.
     - Re-index must not touch the whole inbox/ → only explicit --samples;
     sample records removed after report in default mode.
     - Discord: MESSAGE CONTENT intent off / rate limits / dup replies →
     intent-off detection + hint, Retry-After backoff, after cursor dedup.
     - Ambiguous/empty/timeout insurer reply → treated as skip (smaller valid
     schema, never guess); summary lists skipped fields.
     - No sample docs → onboard degrades to domain-only drafting and reports
     "authored, unverified"; review errors cleanly.

     Verification

     - Linter unit checks (no model/network): COI & FNOL → zero violations +
     roundtrip_ok; negative fixtures ($ref, oneOf, nested object,
     array-of-scalars, array-item-with-array, bad x_natural_key, colliding
     title) each → ≥1 violation.
     - Console onboarding: drop 1–2 born-digital sample PDFs of a new type (e.g.
     an insurance binder) in samples_binder/; python schema_agent.py onboard 
     "<desc>" --samples samples_binder --channel console; answer the gap
     prompts; expect config/BinderOfInsurance.schema.json written,
     lint/round-trip logged, samples re-indexed, gate report shows 1–4 pass / 6
     n/a.
     - Corpus stays green: default run leaves repo pristine — diff 
     config/active.schema.json config/coi.schema.json empty, and python 
     verifier.py exits 0 (existing COI+FNOL PASS/QUEUED as before).
     - review pass: with COI active, review --samples <real COIs> → data-driven
     questions; answer "no" to all → final schema unchanged, lint passes, corpus
     green.
     - Discord live (only if DISCORD_BOT_TOKEN+DISCORD_CHANNEL_ID set): re-run
     onboarding --channel discord; bot posts the question, human reply advances
     the agent; double-reply shows dedup; network drop surfaces a clean error
     without corrupting config/.

     Build sequence

     1. schema_util linter/round-trip/collision + unit checks. 2.
     channels/base.py + console.py + factory. 3. schema_agent.py end-to-end on
     the console channel (verify console onboarding + corpus-green + review). 4.
     channels/discord_channel.py (verify live if a token exists). 5.
     channels/whatsapp.py stub + .env.example/requirements.txt/README/CLAUDE.md
     docs.

  current imports and tail to append cleanly.

      157  def required_paths(active: dict) -> List[str]:
      158      """Top-level required field names (for human-readable diag
           nostics)."""
      159      return list(active.get("required", []))
      160 +                                                              
      161 +                                                              
      162 +# ----- guarding model-authored schemas ----------------------
          +--------------                                                
      163 +# An agent (schema_agent.py) authors new schemas. These functi
          +ons are the                                                   
      164 +# formal statement of the shape the pipeline above supports — 
          +they keep a                                                   
      165 +# generated schema from silently breaking classify()/envelope_
          +schema()/                                                     
      166 +# value_layer()/iter_fields(). Nothing is activated unless it 
          +passes them.                                                  
      167 +                                                              
      168 +_UNSUPPORTED_KEYWORDS = (                                     
      169 +    "$ref", "oneOf", "anyOf", "allOf", "if", "then", "else", "
          +not",                                                         
      170 +    "patternProperties", "dependencies", "dependentSchemas",  
      171 +)                                                             
      172 +_SCALAR_TYPES = ("string", "number", "integer")               
      173 +                                                              
      174 +                                                              
      175 +def _leaf_violations(label: str, leaf: dict) -> List[str]:    
      176 +    out = []                                                  
      177 +    for kw in _UNSUPPORTED_KEYWORDS:                          
      178 +        if kw in leaf:                                        
      179 +            out.append(f"{label}: unsupported keyword '{kw}'")
      180 +    if "const" in leaf or "enum" in leaf:                     
      181 +        return out  # const/enum leaves are fine — classify() 
          +handles them                                                  
      182 +    t = leaf.get("type")                                      
      183 +    if t is None:                                             
      184 +        out.append(f"{label}: leaf needs a 'type' (or const/en
          +um)")                                                         
      185 +    elif t not in _SCALAR_TYPES:                              
      186 +        out.append(f"{label}: unsupported leaf type {t!r} (use
          + string/number/integer, enum, or const)")                     
      187 +    return out                                                
      188 +                                                              
      189 +                                                              
      190 +def lint_authored_schema(schema: dict) -> List[str]:          
      191 +    """Return a list of shape violations (empty == valid). The
          + supported shape:                                             
      192 +    draft-07 object of scalar leaves + at most one level of ar
          +ray-of-objects of                                             
      193 +    scalar leaves, plus optional x_natural_key naming a scalar
          + field."""                                                    
      194 +    if not isinstance(schema, dict):                          
      195 +        return ["schema is not a JSON object"]                
      196 +    v: List[str] = []                                         
      197 +    if schema.get("$schema") != "http://json-schema.org/draft-
          +07/schema#":                                                  
      198 +        v.append("$schema must be 'http://json-schema.org/draf
          +t-07/schema#'")                                               
      199 +    if not isinstance(schema.get("title"), str) or not schema.
          +get("title", "").strip():                                     
      200 +        v.append("title must be a non-empty string")          
      201 +    if schema.get("type") != "object":                        
      202 +        v.append("top-level type must be 'object'")           
      203 +    for kw in _UNSUPPORTED_KEYWORDS:                          
      204 +        if kw in schema:                                      
      205 +            v.append(f"(root): unsupported keyword '{kw}'")   
      206 +                                                              
      207 +    props = schema.get("properties")                          
      208 +    if not isinstance(props, dict) or not props:              
      209 +        v.append("schema must have a non-empty 'properties' ob
          +ject")                                                        
      210 +        props = props if isinstance(props, dict) else {}      
      211 +                                                              
      212 +    for name, prop in props.items():                          
      213 +        if not isinstance(prop, dict):                        
      214 +            v.append(f"{name}: property must be an object")   
      215 +            continue                                          
      216 +        if _is_array_of_objects(prop):                        
      217 +            for kw in _UNSUPPORTED_KEYWORDS:                  
      218 +                if kw in prop or kw in prop.get("items", {}): 
      219 +                    v.append(f"{name}: unsupported keyword '{k
          +w}' in array")                                                
      220 +            item_props = prop.get("items", {}).get("properties
          +")                                                            
      221 +            if not isinstance(item_props, dict) or not item_pr
          +ops:                                                          
      222 +                v.append(f"{name}: array items must be objects
          + with 'properties'")                                          
      223 +            else:                                             
      224 +                for sub, leaf in item_props.items():          
      225 +                    if not isinstance(leaf, dict):            
      226 +                        v.append(f"{name}[].{sub}: must be an 
          +object")                                                      
      227 +                    elif leaf.get("type") in ("array", "object
          +") or "properties" in leaf or "items" in leaf:                
      228 +                        v.append(f"{name}[].{sub}: nested arra
          +ys/objects inside an array item are not supported")           
      229 +                    else:                                     
      230 +                        v += _leaf_violations(f"{name}[].{sub}
          +", leaf)                                                      
      231 +        elif prop.get("type") == "array":                     
      232 +            v.append(f"{name}: arrays must be arrays-of-object
          +s (array-of-scalars is not supported)")                       
      233 +        elif prop.get("type") == "object" or "properties" in p
          +rop:                                                          
      234 +            v.append(f"{name}: nested objects are not supporte
          +d (scalar leaves + one array-of-objects only)")               
      235 +        else:                                                 
      236 +            v += _leaf_violations(name, prop)                 
      237 +                                                              
      238 +    nk = schema.get("x_natural_key")                          
      239 +    if nk is not None:                                        
      240 +        if nk not in props:                                   
      241 +            v.append(f"x_natural_key '{nk}' must name a top-le
          +vel property")                                                
      242 +        elif _is_array_of_objects(props.get(nk, {})):         
      243 +            v.append(f"x_natural_key '{nk}' must be a scalar f
          +ield, not an array")                                          
      244 +                                                              
      245 +    for r in schema.get("required", []):                      
      246 +        if r not in props:                                    
      247 +            v.append(f"required field '{r}' is not in properti
          +es")                                                          
      248 +    return v                                                  
      249 +                                                              
      250 +                                                              
      251 +def _synthetic_envelope(schema: dict) -> dict:                
      252 +    """A minimal filled envelope mirroring the schema, for the
          + round-trip check."""                                         
      253 +    def cell(kind: str) -> dict:                              
      254 +        val = 0 if kind == "number" else ("2026-01-01" if kind
          + == "date" else "x")                                          
      255 +        return {"value": val, "confidence": 0.9, "source": {"p
          +age": 1, "text_span": "x"}, "needs_review": False}            
      256 +                                                              
      257 +    env: Dict = {}                                            
      258 +    for name, prop in schema.get("properties", {}).items():   
      259 +        if _is_array_of_objects(prop):                        
      260 +            env[name] = [{sub: cell(classify(s)) for sub, s in
          + prop["items"].get("properties", {}).items()}]                
      261 +        else:                                                 
      262 +            env[name] = cell(classify(prop))                  
      263 +    return env                                                
      264 +                                                              
      265 +                                                              
      266 +def roundtrip_ok(schema: dict) -> Tuple[bool, str]:           
      267 +    """Behavioral proof the schema won't break the pipeline: b
          +uild a synthetic                                              
      268 +    envelope and run envelope_schema/value_layer/iter_fields w
          +ith no exception,                                             
      269 +    and confirm every top-level field is reachable via iter_fi
          +elds."""                                                      
      270 +    try:                                                      
      271 +        env = _synthetic_envelope(schema)                     
      272 +        envelope_schema(schema)                               
      273 +        value_layer(env, schema)                              
      274 +        seen = {path.split("[")[0].split(".")[0] for path, _w,
          + _k in iter_fields(env, schema)}                              
      275 +        missing = [f for f in schema.get("properties", {}) if 
          +f not in seen]                                                
      276 +        if missing:                                           
      277 +            return False, f"fields not reachable via iter_fiel
          +ds: {missing}"                                                
      278 +        return True, "ok"                                     
      279 +    except Exception as exc:  # pragma: no cover - defensive  
      280 +        return False, f"{type(exc).__name__}: {exc}"          
      281 +                                                              
      282 +                                                              
      283 +def title_collision(schema: dict, config_dir: str, exclude_pat
          +h: Optional[str] = None) -> Optional[str]:                    
      284 +    """Path of an existing (non-active) schema sharing this ti
          +tle, or None.                                                 
      285 +    The verifier keys schemas by title globally, so a duplicat
          +e would mis-route                                             
      286 +    existing records. exclude_path skips the file we're (re)wr
          +iting."""                                                     
      287 +    title = schema.get("title")                               
      288 +    if not title:                                             
      289 +        return None                                           
      290 +    for p in glob.glob(os.path.join(config_dir, "*.schema.json
          +")):                                                          
      291 +        if os.path.basename(p) == "active.schema.json":       
      292 +            continue                                          
      293 +        if exclude_path and os.path.abspath(p) == os.path.absp
          +ath(exclude_path):                                            
      294 +            continue                                          
      295 +        try:                                                  
      296 +            if load_schema(p).get("title") == title:          
      297 +                return p                                      
      298 +        except Exception:                                     
      299 +            continue                                          
      300 +    return None

      46 +## Configure what to collect (the schema-authoring agent)      
      47 +The schema config doesn't have to be hand-written. `schema_agen
         +t.py` is an agent that **designs the config for what an insurer
         + needs to collect**: it proposes a complete field set for a doc
         + type, scans sample PDFs to flag salient data it isn't yet capt
         +uring, and **chats with the insurer to confirm the gaps** befor
         +e applying them — then validates the schema, activates it, and 
         +re-runs the pipeline to prove it works.                        
      48 +```bash                                                        
      49 +# Author a NEW doc type from a description + sample PDFs (asks 
         +you about uncertain fields)

         +ier, policy number, effective/expiration dates, coverage + limi
         +t, premium" \

         + console

      55 +- It chats over a **pluggable channel** — `console` (offline de
         +fault), `discord` (set `DISCORD_BOT_TOKEN`/`DISCORD_CHANNEL_ID`
         + in `.env`), or `whatsapp` (Twilio, a documented stretch). See 
         +`.env.example`.                                                
      56 +- It's **builder-side**: it authors `config/<DocType>.schema.js
         +on` and re-runs the existing pipeline — it never queries the in
         +dex. Generated schemas are linted against the supported shape a
         +nd round-tripped through the pipeline before activation (`schem
         +a_util.lint_authored_schema`); nothing is written or activated

         +s 1–4 (no answer-key needed). By default `onboard` restores `ac
         +tive=COI` and removes the sample records afterward, leaving onl
         +y the new `config/*.schema.json`; `--keep` leaves it live for t
         +he viewer.

⏺ Update(CLAUDE.md)
  ⎿  Added 1 line
      31  - **Review-queue records are NOT held to full schema conformanc
          e.** An illegible required field (the reason a degraded scan is
           queued) makes strict `pass` False but the record is still run-
          acceptable (`run_ok`) via a routing bar: grounding + no-fabrica
          tion + correct flagging. Indexed records must pass every gate.
      32  - **On-disk memory:** `.claude/notes.md` is loaded at the start
           of every extraction and appended on each self-corrected failur
          e. It is a live runtime file — paths in `extract.py` (`_read_no
          tes`) and `workflow.py` (`NOTES`) point at `.claude/notes.md`.
      33  - **Distractors the extractor must avoid** (also in `.claude/no
          tes.md`): ISSUE date ≠ revision/printed/signature dates; policy
          _number ≠ certificate/quote/NAIC/claim/police numbers or prior-
          carrier policy; `limit` = PRIMARY per-occurrence only (GL/Umbre
          lla `Each Occurrence`, Auto `Combined Single Limit`, WC `E.L. E
          ach Accident`, Professional `Each Claim`) — never aggregates; c
          ertificate_holder/insured ≠ additional-insured names.
      34 +- **Authored schemas must stay in the supported shape** (draft-
         +07 object of scalar leaves + at most one array-of-objects + `x_
         +natural_key`; NO `$ref`/`oneOf`/nested objects/array-of-scalars
         +). `schema_util.lint_authored_schema` + `roundtrip_ok` + `title
         +_collision` enforce this; `schema_agent.py` writes/activates no
         +thing unless they pass (with a model-retry-on-invalid loop). Ti
         +tles must be unique (the verifier keys schemas by title). `onbo
         +ard` defaults to restoring `active=COI` + removing sample recor
         +ds (use `--keep` for a live demo); `review` adds fields as OPTI
         +ONAL so existing records of an edited type still validate.

⏺ Done — the config-authoring agent is built, verified end-to-end, and pushed.
  Working tree is clean and verifier.py still exits 0.

  What shipped

  schema_agent.py — an agent that designs the schema config for what an insurer
  needs to collect:
  - onboard "<desc>" --samples <dir> — drafts a complete field set (domain
  knowledge) and scans the sample PDFs for salient data it isn't capturing
  (data-driven), asks the insurer about each gap, applies the confirmed fields,
  validates, activates, re-indexes the samples, and reports the verifier's
  gates.
  - review --samples <dir> — a data-driven gap pass on the active schema ("what
  recurring data am I missing?").

  channels/ — pluggable messaging: console (offline default), discord (two-way
  over REST + polling via requests, no websocket), whatsapp (Twilio stretch
  stub). get_channel() falls back to console if creds are missing, so it never
  hard-fails.

  schema_util.py — lint_authored_schema / roundtrip_ok / title_collision enforce
  the pipeline's supported shape; the agent writes/activates nothing unless
  they pass, with a model-retry-on-invalid loop.

  Verified (console channel, real model calls)

  - onboard authored config/InsuranceBinder.schema.json (16 fields), asked 6 
  data-driven gap questions each grounded in the sample text, re-indexed both
  binders → gates 1–4 pass, then restored active=COI and removed the sample
  records. verifier.py still exits 0.
  - review found 5 plausible uncaptured COI fields, asked, and (on "no") left
  the schema unchanged.
  - tests/test_schema_lint.py passes — both real schemas lint clean; every
  unsupported construct ($ref, oneOf, nested objects, array-of-scalars, bad
  x_natural_key, title collision) is rejected.

  It stays builder-side (authors config, re-runs the pipeline; never queries the
  index), so it extends the config-swap story without drifting into the
  chat-with-index/dashboard territory the brief warns against.

⏺ Done — amend/rename/retype handling is added, verified, and pushed.

  What changed

  Free-text replies are now interpreted by the model into structured decisions
  (confirmed + final field name + leaf type), instead of plain yes/no:
  - "yes, call it effective date" → confirms and renames the field to
  effective_date (the exact case you hit in Discord).
  - "yes, make it a number" / "and it should be a date" → confirms and retypes
  the leaf (number / string+format:date).
  - Plain "no" / "skip" / "" / "maybe later" → declined; "i guess so" →
  confirmed.
  - Deterministic yes/no + regex-rename fallback if the model is unavailable, so
  it degrades gracefully.

  _ask_gaps now collects the raw replies, _resolve_decisions interprets them,
  and _apply adds confirmed fields under their (possibly renamed) name as
  optional.

  Verification

  - 17 reply variants interpreted correctly in direct tests (confirm, decline,
  rename, retype, weak-yes, empty, non-committal).
  - A 12-judge adversarial workflow (one independent fresh-context judge per
  variant) flagged 0 unfaithful interpretations —
  {"total":12,"judged":12,"unfaithful":[]}.
  - schema_agent imports + CLI OK; schema-lint unit checks still pass.

  Committed and pushed to main.

  Two optional next steps

  1. See it live in Discord — I can re-run a short onboard --channel discord so
  you watch the rename get honored end-to-end (reply "yes, call it X" to a
  question and see the field land as x in the authored schema). Say the word and
  watch #insurance-agent.
  2. Clean up the demo state — active.schema.json is still on the binder schema
  and there are leftover index/BINDER-* records + duplicate binder schemas
  (InsuranceBinder, InsuranceBinderConfirmation) from testing. Want me to reset
  to active=COI, remove the binder records, and keep just one binder schema (or
  none)?

  Which would you like — the live Discord re-run, the cleanup, both, or neither?

       7  - `limit` = the PRIMARY per-occurrence limit only (see `config/
          answer-key.json` `_comment` for the per-coverage mapping).
       8  - Ignore the distractors listed in `goal.md` (revision/printed/
          signature dates, prior-carrier/quote/cert/claim/police numbers,
           additional-insured names, aggregate sub-limits).
       9  
      10 +## Cross-line field disambiguation (applies to any insurance do
         +c type)                                                        
      11 +- **Per-occurrence / each-claim limit ≠ aggregate limit.** Per-
         +occurrence (`Each Occurrence`, `Combined Single Limit`, `E.L. E
         +ach Accident`, `Each Claim`) is the max for one event; aggregat
         +e (`General Aggregate`, `Aggregate`, `Products-Comp/Op Agg`) is
         + the cap across the whole term. The headline `*_limit` is the p
         +er-occurrence one; capture aggregate only in a field explicitly
         + named for it.                                                 
      12 +- **Claims-made vs occurrence:** a claims-made policy has a `Re
         +troactive Date` — capture it as `format:date` when present; occ
         +urrence policies do not.                                       
      13 +- **Deductible ≠ Self-Insured Retention (SIR):** both are insur
         +ed-pays-first amounts but distinct fields; don't merge.        
      14 +- **Named Insured ≠ Additional Insured:** capture the named ins
         +ured (the policyholder), never the additional-insured / certifi
         +cate-holder / project-owner.                                   
      15 +- **NAIC # is the carrier identifier**, never a policy number; 
         +**SIC/NAICS** are the insured's industry codes, not coverage da
         +ta.                                                            
      16 +- Document types are distinct: a **Binder** (temporary proof, h
         +as effective/expiration), a **Dec Page** (policy summary), and 
         +a **Certificate of Insurance** (third-party evidence) carry ove
         +rlapping fields but are different `document_type`s.            
      17 +                                                               
      18  ## Certificate of Insurance (COI)
      19  - `issue_date` = the header `DATE ISSUED (MM/DD/YYYY)` value ON
          LY. Not `REVISION DATE`, not `FORM PRINTED`, not the page-2 sig
          nature `Date:` (they often share or nearly share the value — do
          n't be fooled).
      20  - `policy_number` / `effective_date` / `expiration_date` come f
          rom each coverage's `POLICY NUMBER` / `POLICY EFF` / `POLICY EX
          P` row. NOT `CERTIFICATE NUMBER` (CRT-…), `MASTER QUOTE REF` (Q
          -…), `NAIC #`, `REVISION`, or a prior-carrier policy named in t
          he Description of Operations (e.g. "Prior carrier: … policy EI-
          99001").

      126 +def _acord_hint(description: str) -> str:                     
      127 +    """Return an advisory prior for the matched doc type, or '
          +' if none matches                                             
      128 +    (keeps the prompt tight). Disabled via SCHEMA_AGENT_NO_PRI
          +ORS=1 for A/B eval."""                                        
      129 +    if os.environ.get("SCHEMA_AGENT_NO_PRIORS"):              
      130 +        return ""                                             
      131 +    d = " " + (description or "").lower() + " "               
      132 +    for p in ACORD_PRIORS.values():                           
      133 +        if any(k in d for k in p["kw"]):                      
      134 +            return (                                          
      135 +                "\nDOMAIN PRIOR (ADVISORY — still ask the insu
          +rer; confirmed fields are added as "                          
      136 +                "OPTIONAL; do NOT force any of these into requ
          +ired[]):\n"                                                   
      137 +                f"- This resembles a {p['label']}. Such docume
          +nts typically capture: {p['fields']}\n"                       
      138 +                f"- Suggested x_natural_key: {p['natural_key']
          +}.\n"                                                         
      139 +                "- If several repeating sub-records exist, mod
          +el only the SINGLE most-repeating one as "                    
      140 +                "the array-of-objects and flatten the rest to 
          +scalars (the schema allows ONE array)."                       
      141 +            )                                                 
      142 +    return ""                                                 
      143 +                                                              
      144 +                                                              
      145  # ------------------------------------------------------------
           --------------
      146  # helpers
      147  # ------------------------------------------------------------
           --------------

  issue_date — a binder has none), added answer-key ground truth. verifier.py

  grading. Live at https://viewer-puce-phi.vercel.app.

  Move 2 — --route schema selector (the per-insurer lever)

  router.py classifies each inbound PDF's document_type (grounded) and
  auto-selects the matching schema, so a mixed inbox "just works" with no manual
  config swap — the real "adjusts per insurance company" capability. A thin
  stage (not an agent), passing the schema into process_doc (no racy cp). The
  selection is accuracy-graded: router.py --grade passes on all 9 docs (incl.
  the OCR'd scan); workflow.py --route proven end-to-end (routed a FNOL against
  FirstNoticeOfLoss while active=COI).

  Skill-wiring — kept what's proven, rejected what isn't

  - Kept (notes.md): cross-line field disambiguation (from the glossary) +
  binder distractor rules validated against the indexed binder records — future
  doc types inherit field discipline with zero code.
  - Kept (one line): the multi-array flattening rule in SUPPORTED_SHAPE_RULES
  (fixes the COPE/claims lint risk the critic flagged).
  - Rejected (honestly): the ACORD "domain priors" for the draft prompts. The
  critic demanded I gate them behind a measurement — my A/B showed Opus 4.8 
  already surfaces retroactive_date/aggregate/deductible without them, so they
  were pure prompt bloat. Didn't ship them.

  The honest verdict on your two options

  - "Use them for the schema-authoring agent" — modest. The model is already
  strong enough that most domain priors are redundant; the durable win was the
  notes.md extraction discipline, not authoring-prompt priors.
  - "Create more agents for per-insurer adjustment" — the real win, but as a
  stage, not an agent: the router is what makes the pipeline adapt to each
  insurer's document mix. The critic correctly downgraded both proposed "agents"
  to a helper + a (deferred) schema_agent profile subcommand.

  Task A — insurer-profile (two mock insurers, mocked data, end-to-end)

  Storage (config-driven, no code change to add an insurer):
  config/profiles/<id>.json — kept separate from doc schemas so schemas stay in
  the supported shape. Each profile holds the per-insurer process axes:
  - departments (their codes), lob_taxonomy (line_of_business → department),
  market_type (admitted/surplus), and a mocked synthetic agency_codes map
  (producer name → internal code). config/profiles/active.json is the active one
  (mirrors the active.schema.json swap pattern).

  Authoring: python schema_agent.py profile <id> [--samples <dir>] [--channel 
  discord] — the agent drafts a profile from a description + samples, confirms
  the key axes with the insurer over the channel (reusing the channel layer + a
  profile-specific confirm pass), validates with a small profile linter, writes
  config/profiles/<id>.json.

  Router consumption: when a profile is active, router.route_one enriches its
  decision with department (= lob_taxonomy[line_of_business]), agency_code (mock
  lookup on the producer), and market_type. So the same COI routes differently 
  per insurer — Insurer A (admitted MGA): GL+professional → CL; Insurer B (E&S
  wholesaler): professional → SPEC, GL → CAS. Shown via CLI (router.py --doc 
  COI-1003 --profile A vs B).

  Grading/proof: the model-inferred part (document_type) stays accuracy-graded
  as today; the profile enrichment is a deterministic config lookup, so a small
  tests/test_profiles.py checks LOB→department + agency resolution per insurer
  (no model needed).

  Viewer hook (non-destructive): router.py --annotate --profile <id> writes a
  routing block (department, agency_code, profile) onto existing records
  deterministically from already-extracted values — no re-extraction, so the
  green index + reconciliation are untouched and the verifier ignores the extra
  key.

  The two mock insurers ship as config/profiles/harborview-mga.json (admitted)
  and config/profiles/sierra-surplus.json (E&S), with synthetic agency codes.

  Task B — Polished record viewer (editorial, record-centric, no dashboard)

  Enhance the existing self-contained static viewer/index.html (still no build,
  still Vercel-deployable):
  1. Doc-type grouping + filter chips (COI · FNOL · Binder, with counts) — makes
  the config-swap/router story visible: 3 types, one pipeline.
  2. Grounding made visual — click a field to highlight its verbatim source
  span; a small "grounded ✓" affordance tying value ↔ span.
  3. Spotlight the diff — the reconciled COI-1001_UPDATED gets a prominent
  before→after panel.
  4. Spotlight the self-catch — the Pinecrest scan's flagged fields get a clear
  "needs review — auto-routed" treatment (the autonomy beat).
  5. Routing/profile chip — per record, show document_type → department · agency
  · profile from Task A's routing block.
  6. Editorial polish — warm paper, serif display headers, refined
  hierarchy/spacing/accents; a one-line trust banner (verifier exits 0 / every
  field proven). Not a dashboard.

  Build order: Task A first (so routing metadata exists), then Task B (consumes
  it), then regenerate + redeploy to the live URL.

  Does this design look right for both? Once you confirm, I'll build Task A,
  then Task B, verifying and committing each.

      190 +def _record_lob_and_producer(record: dict):                   
      191 +    """Derive a representative line_of_business + producer nam
          +e from a record's                                             
      192 +    already-extracted values (no model call), so a profile can
          + enrich it."""                                                
      193 +    reg = V._schemas_by_title()                               
      194 +    schema = reg.get(record.get("schema_title"))              
      195 +    if not schema:                                            
      196 +        return None, None                                     
      197 +    vals = S.value_layer(record.get("extraction", {}), schema)
      198 +    lob = None                                                
      199 +    cov = vals.get("coverages")                               
      200 +    if isinstance(cov, list) and cov:                         
      201 +        lob = cov[0].get("coverage_type")          # COI: prim
          +ary coverage                                                  
      202 +    elif vals.get("coverage_type"):                           
      203 +        lob = vals.get("coverage_type")             # binder  
      204 +    elif vals.get("loss_type"):                               
      205 +        lob = vals.get("loss_type")                 # FNOL (re
          +solve_department maps it)                                     
      206 +    producer = vals.get("producer") or vals.get("producing_age
          +ncy")                                                         
      207 +    return lob, producer                                      
      208 +

      576 +def profile_cmd(insurer_id: str, description: str, samples_dir
          +: Optional[str],                                              
      577 +                channel_name: str, activate: bool) -> int:    
      578 +    channel = get_channel(channel_name)                       
      579 +    samples = _list_pdfs(samples_dir)                         
      580 +    sample_texts = _sample_texts(samples)                     
      581 +    channel.send(f"Setting up a routing profile for {insurer_i
          +d}. I'll propose how your inbound "                           
      582 +                 "documents should be triaged and confirm the 
          +details with you.")                                           
      583 +                                                              
      584 +    print("• drafting profile (invoking model) …")            
      585 +    feedback, prof = None, None                               
      586 +    for attempt in range(1, MAX_RETRIES + 1):                 
      587 +        draft = _draft_profile(insurer_id, description, sample
          +_texts, feedback)                                             
      588 +        draft["insurer_id"] = insurer_id  # authoritative     
      589 +        violations = profiles.lint_profile(draft)             
      590 +        if not violations:                                    
      591 +            prof = draft                                      
      592 +            break                                             
      593 +        print(f"  [profile retry {attempt}] invalid: {violatio
          +ns}")                                                         
      594 +        feedback = "\n".join(f"- {v}" for v in violations)    
      595 +    if not prof:                                              
      596 +        channel.send("I couldn't produce a valid profile; noth
          +ing was changed.")                                            
      597 +        return 1                                              
      598 +                                                              
      599 +    # confirm the key axes over the channel                   
      600 +    summary = (f"Proposed profile for {prof['display_name']} (
          +{prof['market_type']} market): "

          +g. "                                                          
      602 +               + ", ".join(f"{k}→{v}" for k, v in list(prof['l
          +ob_taxonomy'].items())[:4])                                   
      603 +               + f"; default {prof.get('default_department')}.
          +")                                                            
      604 +    reply = channel.ask(summary + " Does this match your setup
          +? (yes, or describe corrections)",                            
      605 +                        timeout=CHANNEL_TIMEOUT)              
      606 +    if reply and not _affirmative(reply):                     
      607 +        print("  [profile] applying correction …")            
      608 +        prof2 = _draft_profile(insurer_id, description + "\nIN
          +SURER CORRECTION: " + reply, sample_texts)

      610 +        if not profiles.lint_profile(prof2):                  
      611 +            prof = prof2                                      
      612 +

  updates reconcile with a diff, and the same documents adapt to each insurer's
  departments/agency codes via a config-only profile — all visible on the live
  editorial viewer. Good place to land for the demo; want me to do anything else
  before you present?

⏺ Three solid additions — and they genuinely sharpen the "emailed PDFs →
  verified records, configurable per insurer" story. Before I build, a few
  decisions matter because two of them bump into real constraints I should flag:

  - The live viewer is a static page (no server) — a mock email inbox, PDF
  viewing, and a chat transcript all work great bundled into it. A live, 
  interactive chat is the exception: it needs a small backend (a Vercel
  serverless function calling the model + the API key in Vercel), which is a
  bigger build.
  - Anti-scope guardrail: the hackathon brief bans a "chat with your index" box
  (it reads as basic-RAG). The chat you want is the insurer ↔ config-authoring 
  agent (the schema/profile onboarding conversation I built) — that's allowed
  and on-story. I'll frame it explicitly as that, never as querying the index.

  Let me lock the scope:

⏺ User answered Claude's questions:
  ⎿  · The chat (insurer ↔ the config-authoring agent — NOT 'chat with your 
     index'). How should it work in the UI? → Live backend chat
     · The mock email inbox — how interactive? → Interactive flow (Recommended)
     · Viewing the source PDFs — how deep? → PDF + span highlight (Recommended)

⏺ Got it — live backend chat, interactive inbox flow, and
  PDF-with-span-highlight. This is a real build that changes the deploy from a
  static page to a Vercel project with a serverless function, so let me lay out
  the design and confirm before I build it.

  The demo becomes one guided page: Inbox → Record → Configure

  1. Mock email inbox (interactive). A left "inbox" pane of synthetic emails —
  sender, subject, PDF attachment (the corpus docs). Click an email → an
  animated pipeline run (extract → verify → route) → the verified record reveals
  on the right. The records are the real verifier-passed outputs (the animation
  just reveals them; it doesn't re-run the model live, so it's reliable on
  stage).

  2. Record view + PDF with span highlight. The editorial record (already
  built). Now clicking a field opens the actual source PDF to the cited page via
  PDF.js and highlights the verbatim span — value ↔ real document, the
  strongest grounding proof. (PDFs get bundled into the deploy; the image-only
  scan shows page-view only, no text layer.)

  3. Live config-agent chat. A chat panel where you type as the insurer and the
  config-authoring agent responds — proposes fields for a doc type, asks about
  gaps, shows the schema it's building. Backed by a Vercel serverless function
  (api/chat.js) that calls the Anthropic API with the config-agent system
  prompt. Strictly the onboarding/config agent — never "chat with your index"
  (stays clear of the RAG ban). The API key lives server-side in Vercel env
  (I'll set it via the CLI; never exposed to the browser).

  4. Clear story / flexibility framing. A concise top narrative: "Insurance 
  teams hand-key emailed PDFs for weeks. Here: the email arrives, every field is
  extracted with its source proof, uncertain ones self-route to review, and one
  config file — authored by chatting with the agent — re-targets the whole 
  pipeline to any insurer's documents." Plus a visible "Configurable for any
  insurer" thread tying the chat → schema/profile → routing.

  Architecture change

  - Deploy structure becomes a project root: static index.html + bundled PDFs +
  api/chat.js (Node serverless, calls Anthropic via fetch).
  - I'll set ANTHROPIC_API_KEY in the Vercel project env (server-side) and
  redeploy; the live URL stays the same and public.
  - Light guards on the public endpoint (message-length + turn cap) since it
  calls the model.

  Build order

  1. Bundle PDFs + add PDF.js span-highlight to the record view. 2. Build the
  interactive inbox flow + narrative framing. 3. api/chat.js + the chat
  panel. 4. Restructure deploy, set the Vercel env key, redeploy, verify live
  (chat works, PDFs render, public 200).

  This keeps everything on the one live URL and tells the full story end to end.
  Good to go? (Heads-up: the live chat endpoint will incur model cost per
  message and is the one piece that can fail on stage if the network/API hiccups
  — I'll add a graceful fallback message, but say the word if you'd rather I
  make the chat scripted-playback for reliability.)

      424 +let pdfCache = {};                                            
      425 +async function openPdf(file, page, span, fieldName){          
      426 +  const modal = document.getElementById('modal');             
      427 +  document.getElementById('mTitle').textContent = file;       
      428 +  document.getElementById('mSub').textContent = 'page ' + page
          + + ' · ' + fieldName;

          + the verbatim span this field was grounded to — “' + span + '”
          +';                                                            
      430 +  modal.classList.add('open');                                
      431 +  try{                                                        
      432 +    const doc = pdfCache[file] || (pdfCache[file] = await pdfj
          +sLib.getDocument('pdfs/'+file).promise);                      
      433 +    const pg = await doc.getPage(page);                       
      434 +    const scale = 1.5, viewport = pg.getViewport({scale});    
      435 +    const canvas = document.getElementById('pdfCanvas'), ctx =
          + canvas.getContext('2d');                                     
      436 +    canvas.width = viewport.width; canvas.height = viewport.he
          +ight;                                                         
      437 +    document.getElementById('pdfStage').style.width = viewport
          +.width+'px';                                                  
      438 +    document.getElementById('pdfStage').style.height = viewpor
          +t.height+'px';                                                
      439 +    await pg.render({canvasContext: ctx, viewport}).promise;  
      440 +    // highlight: match text items contained in the (normalize
          +d) span                                                       
      441 +    const layer = document.getElementById('hlLayer'); layer.in
          +nerHTML='';                                                   
      442 +    const norm = s => s.replace(/\s+/g,' ').trim().toLowerCase
          +();                                                           
      443 +    const target = norm(span); let firstTop=null;             
      444 +    const tc = await pg.getTextContent();                     
      445 +    tc.items.forEach(it=>{                                    
      446 +      const t = norm(it.str); if(t.length<2) return;          
      447 +      if(target.includes(t)){                                 
      448 +        const m = pdfjsLib.Util.transform(viewport.transform, 
          +it.transform);                                                
      449 +        const h = Math.hypot(m[2], m[3]); const w = (it.width|
          +|0)*scale;                                                    
      450 +        const left = m[4], top = m[5]-h;                      
      451 +        const box = document.createElement('div'); box.classNa
          +me='hlbox';                                                   
      452 +        box.style.left=left+'px'; box.style.top=top+'px'; box.
          +style.width=Math.max(w,4)+'px'; box.style.height=(h*1.15)+'px'
          +;                                                             
      453 +        layer.appendChild(box); if(firstTop===null||top<firstT
          +op) firstTop=top;                                             
      454 +      }                                                       
      455 +    });                                                       
      456 +    if(firstTop!==null) document.querySelector('.pdf-scroll').
          +scrollTop = Math.max(0, firstTop-80);                         
      457 +  }catch(e){                                                  
      458 +    document.getElementById('mNote').textContent = 'Could not 
          +render this PDF here (the scanned doc is image-only). Span: “'
          ++span+'”';                                                    
      459 +  }

⏺ All three features are built, verified live, and shipped. The story is now
  end-to-end on one URL.

  What's live at https://viewer-puce-phi.vercel.app

  A single guided demo console — Inbox → Record → Configure — that makes the
  whole workflow legible:

  1. Mock email inbox. Synthetic emails arrive with PDF attachments (sender,
  subject, attachment, status). Click one → an animated pipeline run (reading 
  attachment → extracting → verifying → routing) reveals the real
  verifier-passed record. (Fakes the email layer exactly as the brief intends —
  no IMAP.)

  2. Verified record + PDF span-highlight. Each field sits beside its verbatim
  source span; click a span → the actual source PDF opens (PDF.js) and the span 
  is highlighted on the right line — value ↔ real document, the strongest
  grounding proof. The diff and the review-queue self-catch keep their spotlight
  treatments.

  3. Live config-agent chat. A "Configure for your company" drawer where you
  chat with the config-authoring agent (live, via a Vercel serverless function
  api/chat.js → Anthropic API, key server-side only). It proposes fields for a
  new doc type, asks about gaps, respects renames/types, and stays strictly
  config-only — never "chat with your index" (clears the RAG ban).

  4. The story, made explicit. A narrative ribbon — Email arrives → Extract & 
  ground → Verify & route → Configure for any insurer — and the masthead frame
  the weeks-to-seconds, configurable-per-company pitch.

  Verified in production

  - Deploy READY, prod alias 200, public, no console errors.
  - Live chat works through the UI (returned a real ACORD-130 workers-comp
  field-set proposal, with a class-codes/payroll repeating group respecting the
  schema shape).
  - PDF + span highlight works from the deployed /pdfs/ (anchored on value/date
  tokens so it lands precisely).
  - PDF.js pinned with SRI (per the security hook), using the correct cdnjs
  hash.

  State

  Everything committed and pushed to main, working tree clean, docs
  (README/CLAUDE.md) and memory updated with the new deploy shape (the deploy is
  now a Vercel project with a function + bundled PDFs, and the env-key-via-REST
  gotcha is recorded).

  One operational note for the demo: the chat calls the model live, so it needs
  network + the Anthropic credits (you confirmed those) — if you want a
  zero-risk fallback for the stage, I can add a "scripted playback" mode toggle
  alongside the live chat, but as-is it's working. Anything else you'd like
  polished before you present?

⏺ Background security review found: XSS via attribute breakout in onclick
handler in viewer.py

⏺ Valid finding — I'll fix it, not dismiss it. The onclick builds inline JS with
  esc(), which escapes " but not ', so a ' in a field name or filename could
  break out of the single-quoted JS string and inject. With the current
  synthetic corpus the values are clean, but this app's whole premise is
  ingesting arbitrary documents with agent-authored schemas — so untrusted text
  reaching a field name/filename is exactly the threat model. The data-attribute
  + delegated-listener fix is strictly better. Applying it.
